After I have completed for you, O Children, this book, which is the final knowledge in medicine with its completion, and have reached its end in its explanations and its declarations, it seemed good to me to complete it for you with this Treatise which is a part of the operation, that is, of surgery with the hand.
Since the operation with the hand has been neglected in our region and in our time, entirely private: until perhaps its knowledge perished, and its trace was cut off: and nothing remained of it except for small descriptions in the books of the ancients, which changed hands: and error and hesitation befell them, until its intentions were closed, and its power was distanced: It seemed good to me to revive it with the arrangement of this Treatise on it according to the way of exposition, declaration, and abbreviation: and to come with forms of the cautery instruments, and the other instruments of the work: with the addition of declaration and the hastening of what is necessary.
However, the reason why a good artisan of it with his hand is not found in our time is this: because the art of medicine is long, and its author must be exercised beforehand in the knowledge of anatomy, as Galen has recounted, until he knows the aids of the limbs, and their forms, and their conjunction and separation, and has knowledge of the bones, and nerves, and tendons, and their number, and their exits, and the pulsating and quiet veins, and the places of their exits.
And because of that Hippocrates said that a name with a name is much, and with a work is little, and especially in the art of the hand.
We, however, have already spoken of that in the introduction of this book.
Since whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said concerning anatomy is not purged, but inevitably falls into error, by which people are killed: just as I have seen many of those who are formed in this knowledge, and boast about it without knowledge and without experience.
That is because I saw a foolish physician cut an abscess on the neck of a woman, and he cut some arteries in her neck, wherefore the woman's blood flowed until she fell dead in his hands.
And I saw another physician who presumed to extract a stone from a man who was advanced in years, and the stone was large. Therefore, he reached it and extracted it with a fragment of the bladder. Therefore the man died on the third day.
And indeed I had already been called to extract it, and I saw from the size of the stone and the disposition of the sick man that he would die.
And I saw another physician who was receiving payment from a certain Duke of our land for his medical services; and it happened that a black eunuch who was with him suffered a fracture in his leg near the heel; and the physician, in his ignorance, bound the fracture over the wound with pillows and splints with strong constriction, and did not allow the wound any breathing space.
Then he discharged him according to his desires. After that, he dismissed him for a few days, and instructed him not to loosen the bandages.  And he stood like that until his leg and foot became ulcerated and festered and reached ruin.
I was therefore called to him, and I hurried to loosen the bandages; and tranquility followed, and he escaped his pains.
However, the corruption had already taken hold in the limb, and I could not restrain it.
Therefore, the corruption ceased to spread in the limb, until it perished.
And I saw another physician, who pierced the cancerous abscess; and it ulcerated after days, until its malice increased with its owner.
This is because when the cancer is pure from melancholic humor, then one should not attempt to reach it with iron at all, unless it is in a limb that can tolerate its complete excision.
Therefore, children, it is necessary for you to know that surgical intervention is divided into two divisions: namely, intervention associated with health; and intervention with peril in many dispositions.
And I have already aroused in every place of this book, in which intervention is found, in which there is terror and fear.
Therefore, it is necessary for you to beware of it, and to cut it away, lest fools find a way to speak ill of it.
Therefore, receive the measure with care and protection, and your sick with ease and firmness, and use the better way leading through God's grace to health and praiseworthy success; and leave the terrible illnesses of difficult cure; and lift your souls from that which causes you fear, lest hesitation enter upon your faith and your well-being.
For it is more remaining to your glory, and more sublime in this world, and finally to your merits.
For Galen already said in some of his admonitions. Do not treat a bad illness, lest you be called a bad physician.
Now, however, I have divided this Treatise into three Chapters.
First Chapter.
Concerning the cautery with fire, and the cautery with sharp medicine,  headed and arranged from head to foot, and the forms of instruments, and the equipment of the cautery: and everything necessary in the operation.
Second Chapter.
Concerning section and perforation, phlebotomy and cupping, and wounds: and the extraction of arrows, and similar things: and all of it headed and arranged according to the forms of instruments.
Third Chapter.
Concerning restoration, and dislocation, and the treatment of twisting, and similar things: headed and arranged from head to foot, and the forms of instruments.
But before I recount the operation with it, it is necessary that I speak of the quality of its benefits and harms, and in what complexion it is to be employed.
I say therefore, that discourse on the quality of the cautery's benefit and harm is a lengthy and subtle discourse, a matter of knowledge and hidden secret.
Many wise men have also spoken on this, and disagreed on it; and for my part, a little from their sayings suffices me, fearing prolixity.
I say therefore, that the cautery benefits every complexion, whether with matter or without matter, except for the two complexions which are hot without matter and dry without matter.
However, they disagreed on the hot and dry complexion with matter. For some said that the cautery is beneficial in it. And others said the opposite, namely that the cautery is not suitable in the illness which is from heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat, and it is unsuitable for healing from a hot and dry illness with hot and dry [means].
And he who says the opposite said: that through the cautery help is given in every hot and dry illness that occurs in human bodies, because when you compare the human body and its humours to the complexion of fire, you find the human body cold.
And I myself say, through his statement: because experience has already revealed that to me many times.
However, it is not necessary that it come upon that, unless one who is already proven and exercised in the last exercise of the cautery chapter, and has known the diversity of human complexions and the disposition of illnesses within themselves, and their causes, and their accidents, and their duration of time.
However, there is no fear from the remaining complexions; and especially in cold and humid illnesses. For now all physicians have agreed upon them, and they have not disagreed in the help provided by the cautery in those cases.
And know, children, that the secret of healing through cautery with fire, and its goodness over cautery with burning medicine, is that fire is simple, whose action does not reach except the member that is cauterized; and does not harm any other member joined to it, except by a small harm.
However, the action of burning medicine reaches what is separated from the members; and perhaps causes illness of difficult healing in the member, and perhaps kills it.
But fire, because of its subtlety and goodness of its substance, does not do that, unless it overflows.
Now, however, this has become known to us through experience, because of the length of service and study with the art, and our standing upon the truth of things; and because of that I am excused from the length of speech.
And if it were not so, because it is not permitted to this book of mine, I would bring to you the secret hidden in fire, and the quality of its operation on bodies of its expulsion, by which it expels illnesses, demonstrated by philosophical discourse, which would be sharpened by your minds.
And know, children, that they disagree on the time in which the cautery should be performed, and they set a better time for the verus.
And I say that the cautery is suitable at all times, because the harm which is incidental to time is submerged in the benefit which is attracted with the cautery. And especially if the cautery is for pains from necessary, strong, urgent pains, which do not tolerate slowness, because it is feared from them that a greater evil will happen, than the small harm which enters because of time.
And do not let it enter your minds, O children, that which the common people and foolish physicians do not fear, namely that the illness which is cured by cautery does not always return.  And they put this as a consequence, and the matter is not as they think. For the cautery is not, except in the place of medicine, which alters the complexion and dries the humours that are the causes of the pains that occur.
However, the cautery excels over medicine in the speed of its cure, and the virtue of its operation, and the vehemence of its dominion. And it is possible that the illness may return at some time according to the complexion of the infirm person, and the location of his illness, and its strength, and that which is prepared in his body from the aggregation of superfluities in him, and that which arrives at him in his acquisition from foods and similar causes, unless there is a disease in which the cautery is administered.
A subtle illness in a limb of few superfluities and humours, like a toothache, because of the pain, and things similar to it, it is possible that that pain will not return in it. But that happens in few cases.
But truly the common people's statement, that cautery is the last resort of medicine, is a correct statement, not in the sense they intend by it. For they believe that there is no cure which can compare with medicine, nor with anything else after the application of cautery.
However, the matter is the opposite of that. The idea that cautery is the last resort of medicine is not the case unless when we apply methods of treatment in some illnesses, and those treatments do not work; then, at the end of the matter, we administer cautery, and it works.  Then, it follows that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not in the sense understood by the common people and many foolish physicians.
However, the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron.  And they did not say this except because of the equal weight and the high quality of its substance.  And they said that the site of the cautery does not produce pus. But that is not absolutely so, for I have already tested it, and found that it does not do so in some bodies without others.
And cautery with it [gold] is good, and better than with iron, as they said. However, when you apply a cautery of gold in fire, it is not clear to you when it is heated to the desired degree because of the redness of the gold.  And when it approaches the cold, and if you add heat to it, it melts in the fire and turns into sheets.
Therefore, the craftsman falls away from that practice.  And because of this, cautery with iron is faster and more readily available for us, from the straightforwardness of the operation.
And I indeed have already arranged this chapter on cautery, according to chapters, and have arranged them from head to foot, so that they may alleviate the one seeking what they want from it.
Chapter II.
This cauterization benefits by controlling moisture and coldness over the brain, which are two causes of headaches, and the excessive flow of humors from the head to the eyes and ears, and excessive sleep, and toothache, and sore throat; and universally, all illnesses that arise from coldness, such as paralysis, headaches, epilepsy, and apoplexies, and similar illnesses.
The method of cauterization is that you instruct the ill person to be evacuated primarily with a cleansing, dissolving medicine for the head for three or four nights, according to the strength of the ill person, and their age, and their custom.
Then instruct them to shave their head with a razor. Then make him sit between your hands in a square position, so that he has already placed his hands upon his chest.
Then place the root of your palm on the root of his nose between his eyes. Wherever, therefore, your middle finger arrives, mark that place with the cautery.
Then heat the olive-shaped cautery, whose form is this.
Then place it upon the place marked with the cautery, descending, while your hand is gradually tightened, and you will revolve it. Then quickly lift your hand, and look at the place.
If you see now exposed from the bone the size of a head of al-kheil, or the size of a ze'herbi, then lift your hand. And if not, repeat with the iron itself, or with another of the same if it becomes cold, until the bones which I told you appear.
Then take some salt, and dissolve it in water, and soak the cloth in it, and place it over the place, and leave it for three days.
Then place over it the cloth soaked in butter, and leave it over the place until the eschar of the fire is destroyed. Then treat it with the four-drug ointment, until it is healed.
Now they say that the more a wound remains open, the more pus it emits; therefore it is better and more helpful.
And some of them said that the skin should be cauterized down to the bone, and the cautery should be held until a certain thickness of bone is burned.
Then shave off whatever has been burned from the bone, then treat it.
And others say that the cautery should be used to reach the very end, until it makes an impression on the bone, so that the bone falls away, which is done like the shape of a kirate, or a tool that women use for embroidering small letters, and they believe that vapors from the head are expelled from this place, and the wound is left open for a long time.
Then treat it until it heals.
However, these two types of cautery do not seem to me to be suitable for all people, except in some cases, according to the path of caution.
And to leave it, in my opinion, is better for his health.
For the head weakens due to the disruption of its natural continuity, as we have witnessed in other limbs; and especially when the head of the sick person is naturally weak.  And indeed, the first type of cautery is safer and better in my view, and I use it: therefore, operate with it for safety.
Chapter 3.
When chronic pain occurs throughout the head, and it prolongs itself in the sick person, and they use leeches, and cupping, and head-purgations, and oils, and poultices. And especially if it has already been cauterized with the single cautery, which we have described, and none of those things benefit it, then consider. For if the head of the sick person is of strong natural constitution, and not weak, and experiences violent cold, then cauterize with another cautery slightly below the first one. Then cauterize it over every horn of its head with a cautery, so that the skin is not penetrated, and a quantity of bone, as we have described, is exposed. And cauterize it with a single cautery on the back of its head, in the place called the *vas* (blood vessel): and it is the place where a cupping glass is placed; and raise your cautery to this, and do not expose bone. For the sick person experiences intense pain because of that, different from the pain of the other cauterizations of all the head.
And I shall say that this cautery is in its proper place: and it should be a cautery with which the horns of the head are cauterized, and the back of the head with a finer cautery than that used to cauterize the middle of the head.
Chapter Four.
When pain and throbbing occur in a part of the head, or the pain extends to the eye, and the head is purged with cleansing remedies, and the remaining treatment, which I mentioned in the divisions of illnesses, is administered and does not benefit the whole [condition]: then cauterization is performed there in two ways: either cauterization with a burning medicine that is sharp, or with iron.
The cautery with a sharp burning medicine is to take one clove of garlic, and to peel it, and to cut off its extremities from the two sides. Then cut the painful area at a time with a wide lancet, until a place is made under the skin, into which the clove is placed.
Then introduce it into the skin itself, until it is hidden; then tighten above it with a bandage of suitable constriction, and leave it for a period of fifteen hours; then loosen it, and remove the garlic, and leave the wound for two or three days; afterward, place on it a poultice soaked in butter, until the area produces pus; then treat it with ointment until it is healed.
And if you wish, do it with some burning medicines, which I have written in the twelfth treatise, on Burning Medicines.
The cauterization of it with iron, however, is according to this method. A cautery iron, whose shape is this.
And it is called a "clavil," because the shape of its head is like the shape of a nail, in which there is something of curvature, and in its middle there is a small protuberance.
Then place it on the area, and hold your hand; and you turn the iron gradually with speed; and let the quantity that is burned be, from the thickness of the skin, like half of it. And raise your hand, so that the artery, which is below, is not burned, and a flow of blood occurs.
Then soak lint in salt water, and place it over the area, and leave it for three days; then place the lint with butter; afterward treat with ointment until healed.
And if you wish, cauterize this hemicrania with the second cautery's knife edge. And beware of cutting the artery in this hemicrania, not the old one properly.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the old hemicrania.
When treating hemicrania, using what we have said from the preceding treatment, and what we have said in the divisions of illnesses, and if the treatment does not help; and you see from the illness that what we have said about the first cautery with medicine, or with cautery with fire, is not sufficient, then it is necessary to heat the cautery's knife edge until it becomes white after you have marked the place of pain with a line, whose length is half a finger, or nearly that; and place your hand in one place and squeeze it until you cut the artery, and reach the bone.
However, it is necessary for you to beware of the continuation of the jaw, which moves during chewing, lest the side or the nerve that moves it be burned, from which spasm may result.
And be on guard, and careful about the flow of blood from the artery that has been cut. For in its cutting there is fear, and especially for him who does not know what he is doing, and is not diligent nor experienced; and he abandons the operation at the beginning.
And I will come with a reminder of the regimen for the flow of blood arising from the artery according to its manner, and in its place in this book.
If you see from the illness that this cautery is not sufficient for him, and you see the body of the sick man tolerating the cautery in the middle of the head, as we have described, treat the wound until it is healed.
And if you wish, administer the cautery, which we mentioned in the chapter on the extraction of the artery with a cautery having two knives. For cauterization is better than this and more beneficial.
Concerning the method of cauterization in earache.
When pain in the ear occurs from cold, and is treated with remedies, and the rest of the treatment which we mentioned in the division, and the pain is not removed, then apply a cautery with fire; and it is that which is called the Point, whose shape is this.
Then the points, after its ignition, are applied in a circle around the entire ear, as it revolves; or in a circle around each ear, if the pain is in both at the same time. And distance yourself with the cautery a little from the root of the ear, after you have marked the places with encaustic; and let the quantity of the cautery be ten points in each ear, and approximately like that.
Then treat the places until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Torture.
Chapter VII.
Torture that is treated with cauterization is only from the species that occur from phlegm, according to what we have said in the divisions of diseases.
And avoid cauterization of the species that occurs from dryness and nerve spasm.
When you treat this species of torture with emetics, and purges, and gargles, and your treatment is of no avail, then it is necessary that you cauterize the afflicted person with three cauteries: one near the root of the ear, and a second a little lower from its temple, and a third at the junction of the two lips.
And place your cautery on the opposite side of the afflicted part. Because softening does not occur unless in the part that appears healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with a cautery directly at the tip of the upper ear, slightly below the horn of the head: and another at the temple, whose length is according to the length of the thumb. And hold your hand with the cautery until a quantity equal to half the thickness of the skin is burned.
And this is the form of the cautery, and it is a type from a knife, whose form is already mentioned: however, it is not a little thinner than that, as you see: and it is necessary that the knife has a little superfluous thickness in it.
Then treat the places with what preceded, until they are healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in old Apoplexy.
When the apoplexy is chronic, and you have treated it with what we have said, and your treatment does not benefit, and the sick person does not have a fever, then cauterize him with four cauteries over each horn of his head, and with a cautery in the middle of the head, as we have said, and with a cautery at the back of the head, according to what preceded: and the method of cautery should be according to what preceded.
Also, it is cauterized with a cautery on the mouth of the stomach; and it is more of a last resort.
Then, treat it with what has preceded.
Chapter IX.
It is necessary that in the drink, first be given to the sick person large hyerae and pills that cleanse the brain.
Then shave the entire head of the sick person, and place on the back of his head a plaster of mustard described in the treatise on plasters: and apply it several times.
For this is the method of cautery; and do it according to the same order which I said there.
If, therefore, he is healed by it, it is good. If not, then make for him three cauteries on the posterior part of his head, which shall descend from the upper part of the head down to the lower part of the eye: and place between each cautery the thickness of a finger.
Then treat the cautery with what preceded it.
If however you wish an addition, and the sick person is able to tolerate it, then make a cautery in the middle. If you wish an addition, then cauterize him above the two horns.
Then treat him until he is healed: and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the form that was stated previously.
Concerning the method of cauterization in paralysis and softening.
Chapter X.
You should proceed in the cleansing of the head with hygeia, and with what we have said.
Then shave the patient's head; afterward cauterize it with a cautery in the middle of the head, and with a cautery on every horn of the head, and with a cautery on its posterior part, and with three on the vertebrae of the neck.
However, if in the illness there is a need for softening of the body by more than those, and the patient is enduring, and the illness is severe, then cauterize him with four cauteries on the vertebrae of the back, and the last with a cautery, until his skin is largely burned away, and raise your hand. Then treat him until he is healed; and thus is the cautery of Olive.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Epilepsy.
An epileptic is not cauterized, unless that one whose epilepsy is from phlegm.
Therefore, it is necessary that you first cleanse his brain with leeches, and with the other treatment that we have described in the division: when the patient is strong, or is tolerant in accepting medicines.
However, if he is a child who does not tolerate medicines, then a gargle and cleansing mastications for the brain are administered, many days before that with the improvement of foods.
Then shave his head, afterwards cauterize him with one cautery in the middle of the head, according to what preceded in the method; and with another cautery on his occiput, and with a cautery over every horn of his head. If however the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize him with the cauteries that I said for the paralytic, and softening of the body over the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back; and let the cautery be olive-shaped according to the manner that preceded.
If however the patient is a child, then place a delicate cautery, according to this method.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Melancholy.
When the causes of melancholy are corrupted humors and thick phlegm, then cauterize him with the cauteries which we have stated for the paralytic.
And if the cause of the melancholy is an excess inclined to melancholy, and the body of the sick person is damp, then give him in a drink that will cleanse his brain, according to what has preceded in the division; then shave the head of the sick person, and afterwards make a neatly fashioned little roll out of linen, like a circle.
Then place it in the middle of the head; and the sick person, seated upright, should be held in place on all sides.
Then apply the liniment. And it is better made from old sheep's butter. And heat it over a fire with a measured heat, such that a finger can tolerate it when inserted into it. Then apply it in a circle to the middle of his head, and leave it until it cools.
Do this to the sick person once a week, with the rest of his good regimen, until he is healed.
Or if you wish, cauterize it by making many small points on it, while holding the cautery with your hand: indeed, let it be smelled.
For this type of cautery moistens the brain with quality.
Then place a cloth soaked in butter, or chicken fat, upon it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in descending water to the eye.
Chapter XIII.
When you are declared the beginning of water in the eye by the signs, which I have said in the division, then begin and drink the weak one, with that which cleanses his head.
And keep him from all moistures, and make him sit in a bath, fasting for several days.
Then command him to shave his head, and cauterize him in the middle of his head. Then cauterize him above the two temples with two cauteries, if it is the beginning of the descent of water in both eyes simultaneously; or from one side, if it is the beginning of water in one eye; and cut with the cautery all the veins and arteries which are under the skin; and let the cauteries be of the same length as the width of the temples; and beware of the flow of blood.
If you see anything from him, then cut it off immediately with whatever medicine is possible; and I will come with the wisdom that is in the extraction of arteries, and the cutting of them, and the precaution from the flow of blood.
And sometimes it is cauterized on the neck, beneath the two bones, with two cauteries finally applied.
Concerning the method of cauterization in ancient eye diseases.
When the eye's tears are chronic, constant; and are on the veins and arteries that are in the exposed exterior of the head, it is confirmed that it is from cold, phlegmatic superfluities; then cauterize with the same cautery I have described at the beginning of descending water, a cautery in the middle of the head, and two cauteries above the two temples, and two cauteries in the neck under the two bones. And if it needs further treatment, then cauterize it on every side carefully around the eye, above the end of the eyebrow with a small cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterization for nasal foul odor.
When you treat it, with what we have said in the division, and the treatment does not help; then hurry and give the infirm decoctions in a drink for three nights; afterwards shave his head and cauterize it with a middle cautery, with an olive cautery. Then cauterize it with a claw cautery, with two cauteries, above the two eyebrows under the hair a little.
And guard against the artery, lest you strike it.
And this is the shape of the Claw cautery.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in the softening of the eyelid.
When the eyelid of the eye is softened by sickness or moisture, then cauterize the eyelid with a single cautery, with this lunar cautery.
And if you wish, cauterize it above the two eyebrows slightly with two cauteries on every side; and they should be distant from the two temples; and let the length of each cautery be, according to the length of the eyebrow; and do not bring your hand with the cautery, but in accordance with the amount that the third eyelid is to be burned.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the eyelid when the hairs are turned inward, pricking the eye.
The cautery is in it according to two methods: either cautery with fire, or cautery with a burning medicine.
In cautery with fire, first instruct the sick person to remove his hairs, if he is one who cleans them, until they are lengthened and made equal. If, however, they prick him at their origin, then bind his eyes with a bandage so that they do not move until they are born.
When therefore they are born and made equal, then place the sick person's head in your bosom; then mark upon the eyelid of his eyes with ink, a mark that is in the shape of a myrtle leaf; and let the beginning of the mark be near the hairs.
Then place a cloth soaked in egg white, or in psyllium mucilage, over the eye.
Then apply a cautery, whose shape is this.
Then cauterize over the shape which you have marked, gradually in many stages, until the skin's surface, which is like the shape of a myrtle leaf, is entirely burned away.
And the sign of the success of your work is: that if you see the eyelid of the eye already contracting, and the hairs rising near the puncture of the eye.
Therefore raise your hand then, and leave it for three days.
Then place upon it a poultice with butter, until the eschar is removed. Then treat it with ointment until it heals.
If any of the hairs return after an hour, and the eyelid softens, then again cauterize that place, as you did at first.
If however the hairs are in the lower part, then cauterize it until it is raised to its natural place, and made even so that the hairs do not prick the eye.
You should instruct the sick person to let the hairs fall out until they are lengthened and made even. Make a shape of a myrtle leaf from paper on cloth.
Then take from known soap, and from unsoaked lime, one ounce or nearly that of each weight: then grind them together with good trituration, and make it quickly, so that it does not grow cold. Then take some of that from the pan and place it on the paper you made in the shape of a myrtle leaf, and put it on the eyelid of one or two eyes. And place a soaked cloth in egg white under the eye: and let the sick person's head be in your bosom.
And place your index finger on the medicine, and press it for a short time. And you should move it whenever the sick person feels the medicine's biting: for its biting is found to be like fire.
While, therefore, this biting that he finds persists, then release the medicine, and move it with your finger. When, therefore, the biting subsides, then remove the medicine, and wash the eye with water.
And then consider, if you see the eyelid rising, as it rises with a contraction from fire, or with an incision, it is well; and if not, then apply more medicine to the spot where the medicine does not take effect and does not darken, until your operation is equalized and the eye contracts.
Then place upon it Cotum with butter, until the skin of the burn is eradicated. Then treat it with diaphinicon ointment, or another, until it is healed.
And it is necessary for you, at the operation, to observe the utmost care, lest anything of the medicine fall into the eye.
If the eyelid softens after days, and some hair struggles into the eye, then apply medicine again to the place that softens from the eyelid itself, as you did at first. Then treat it until it is healed.
And this is the form of the myrtle leaf.
And know that the eyes of men differ in size and smallness. Therefore, according to that, let your consideration be; and the way of righteousness is not hidden from him who is diligent in this art.
Concerning the method of cauterization in the tear duct fistula.
When you treat a fistula, if, as we have said in the divisions of diseases, your treatment does not help, then, it is necessary to cauterize it according to this method.
Command the sick person to place his head in your lap, and let the attendant hold his head in their hands in such a way that it does not move or shake with his head.
Then place a heated poultice in the white of an egg, or in psyllium mucilage, on his eye; then apply the cautery, whose shape is this.
Let it be concave, like the shape of a vulture's wing feather from one end, with which the cautery is made; and if you want it to penetrate to the other end, and if you want it held upward thus.
However, this concave shape is better for your work.
Then express the fistula, if it is open, and extract the pus from it and dry it; and if it is not open, then open it and extract its pus.
Then place the cautery, which is made very hot, upon it.
And hold your hand near the cautery, from the eye to the nose, so that your hand does not wander or the sick person is disturbed; and place the cautery on the fat of the eye and corrupt it.
If therefore you reach the beginning of your cautery up to the bone, it will be well. And if not, then repeat the cautery once or twice, if you need it, and leave it for three days.
Then apply a compress with butter, and treat it with a drying ointment until it is healed.
If forty days have passed and it is not healed, then apply a sharp, corrosive medicine to it until the bone is exposed, and scrape it according to what appears in its chapter.
And there is another method of cauterizing fistulas, which some of the first [surgeons] said. Direct your attention to the location of the fistula, and cut it open; then place a fine camahan, that is, a fine cannula, of this shape, into the fissure. Pour into it a drachma of liquefied lead, and hold your hand with a good retention cannula, and let the sick person not move at all, so that the liquefied lead does not run or reach his eye.
And it is necessary that you place on the sick person's eye a poultice infused in egg white, or in water.
For lead burns the fistula location and heals it with a remarkable cure.
If the fistula is cured with what we have said about the cautery and treatment, it is good. And if not, then it is necessary to administer the nostril opening, and to return the fistula to the course of the nose, according to what will come to its own proper place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing lip fissures.
Often fissures occur in the lip, called "pili," especially in the lips of children.
Therefore, when you treat these fissures, as we said in the division of diseases, and the treatment does not help, then use a small knife-shaped cautery with fire, according to this form.
And its concavity should be according to the sharpness of the knife.
Then place it, heated, quickly onto the fissures themselves, until the cautery reaches the depth of the fissures.
Then treat it with a cautery, until it heals.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a fistula of the mouth.
When an abscess occurs at the root of the gum, or in the palate, or in the roots of the teeth; then it produces pus, and breaks open; afterward it becomes chronic, and pus runs, and a fistula forms; then you treat it, and treatment does not benefit it, then it is necessary to cauterize with a cautery according to the quantity that fits within the fistula. Then introduce the heated iron into the opening of the fistula, and hold your hand until the heated iron reaches its depth and its farthest point; do it once or twice.
Then treat it afterward, with what we said about treatment, until it is healed.
If therefore the pus is removed, and it heals, it will be good. And if not, then it is necessary to expose the place, and remove the corrupted bone according to what will appear on its surface.
Concerning the method of cauterization in softened gums and teeth.
When the gum softens due to moisture, and the teeth move, and you treat it with medicines, and it does not help, then place the head of the sick person in your lap.
Then, with the cautery, whose form will follow, place the cannula over the tooth, and quickly insert the heated cautery into it; hold your hand there for a short while, until the patient feels the heat of the fire already reaching the root of the tooth.
And lift your hand; then repeat the cautery several times, as you wish.
Then let the patient fill his mouth with salt water, and hold it for one hour; and let him spit it out.
For the moving tooth is strengthened, and the softened gum is tightened, and the corrupted moisture is dried.
On the method of cauterizing in toothache.
When toothache is due to cold, either cold or a worm is in it, and treatment with medicines is of no avail, then cautery is applied to it in two ways: either cautery with butter, or cautery with fire.
However, its cautery with butter is to take cow's butter, and boil it in an iron spoon, or in a vessel. Then take a wick, and wrap it around the tip of the probe. Then immerse it in the boiled butter, and quickly place it on the aching tooth, and hold it until it cools: then repeat it several times, until the power of fire reaches the root of the tooth.
And if you wish, immerse wool, or a wick, in cold butter, and place it on the aching tooth, and place hot iron upon it, until the fire reaches the depth of the tooth's cavity.
Its cauterization with fire is to apply a bronze or iron cannula. And let there be something of its thickness, so that the sharpness of fire does not reach the sick person's bone.
Then apply the cautery, whose form shall come, and place it on that tooth, and hold your hand until the cautery cools.
Do it several times, for the pain will be removed, either on that same day or on another.
And it is necessary, in the application of that cautery, that the sick person fill their mouth with good butter, and hold it for one hour; then spit it out.
And this is the form of the cautery.
Cauterize with whichever extremity of the instrument you can: and this is the form of the cannula.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in ulcers.
When ulcers are from phlegm and cold humors, and are not yielding to digestion by medicines, and the instrument of digestion does not quickly effect them, then use a concave cautery, whose form is this.
Having two open extremities, so that smoke may escape from the cautery at the other extremity, and place it heated upon the abscess once and twice, if it requires this, until it reaches the depth of the abscess.
If the abscess is small, then apply the cautery according to the size of the abscess.
Then leave it for three days, and place upon it a poultice infused in butter, until that which the fire burned is removed.
Then treat it with a tooth ointment, until the form of the cannula is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in hoarseness of voice and constriction of breathing.
When humidities overcome the bronchial passage, and especially when it is with a cold temperament, then it is necessary that the infirm person be evacuated first with loosening medicines.
Then cauterize it in the vicinity of the root of the throat in a depressed place; and be careful not to reach with the cautery the throat itself, nor the skin, except a part of it.
Then cauterize it with another cautery at the junction of the neck at the last vertebra thereof, and let the cautery be narrow according to the manner which preceded.
Then treat it with that which preceded, until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in diseases of the Lung and Cough.
When cough and lung disease are from cold humors, and the sick person does not have a fever, nor consumption, and the disease is old, then cauterize him with two cauteries above the fork in depressed, gentle, empty places. And with another cautery in the middle of the chest between the two breasts: and let the cautery be of the cannula shape as preceded.
And if you wish your cauterization to be by puncturing with a cautery, which is called *Punctum*, whose form preceded in the puncturing of ear pain: and let the punctures be from thirty punctures up to as if another.
Then treat him with what preceded, until he is healed.
And now let the cautery have three branches: according to this form. Therefore, the cauterization is alleviated when you do it with three cauteries at once.
Chapter XXVII.
When the head of the humerus is dislocated because of humours, and does not fix itself in the hour of its return from the dislocation, until it has become accustomed to returning, and then is dislocated by a slight movement, which happens as we have already testified, then you must first reduce the dislocation. Then the patient is to be placed supine on his back, or on his healthy side. Then raise the skin that is in the inner titillico towards the upper parts with the fingers of your left hand: and if the joint is dislocated inwards.
Then, using a cautery with two prongs. Whose shape is this.
Then cauterize the skin until it penetrates it to the other side, and the shape of the cauterization will be with four cauteries.
And sometimes the cauterization is done with a cautery having three prongs, wherefore the shape of the cauterization is then of six cauteries: and the prongs are according to the thinness of the thread.
And this is the shape of the cautery having three prongs.
And sometimes one is added above this manner, wherefore there are eight cauteries.
Then place on the cautery crushed leeks with salt. Then cause the infirm one to adhere to stillness, so that the limb does not move at any time, until it is strengthened.
And if the dislocation is to the upper parts, and rarely does that happen, then cauterize it above the shoulder with a clavicular cautery, or with many cauteries by puncturing.
For the joint is strengthened, and the moisture is removed; and the infirm person is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Stomach.
When cold and many humidities occur in the stomach, until they pull it away from its complexion, and the catarrhs multiply towards it, and frequent methods of treatment do not help: then it is necessary that the sick person be laid on their back, and extend their legs and hands. Then cauterize with three cauteries, one cautery below the breastbone, the size of one finger with a pointed cautery, and two cauteries below it on either side, one cautery each, until the figure of the cauteries becomes triangular. And lengthen between each so that they do not join, when they will make pus.
And let the depth of the cautery be the quantity of two-thirds the thickness of the skin.
And let the figure of the cauteries be according to this form, without addition: and if you wish to cauterize with a large cautery in the middle of the stomach according to this form, let the cautery by which this is done be one according to the form of a circle according to this form.
And the stomach is cauterized by pricking it with that which frightens him with this cautery: and it is, that you mark on the stomach a point according to the quantity that you want with ink; then cauterize it with the cautery of the point; then treat it with the treatment that preceded until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a cold liver.
When pain occurs in the liver from cold and moisture, or from thick wind, until it emerges from its natural complexion by the expulsion of excess, and the sick person is treated with what we have said, and it does not benefit him: then it is necessary that the sick person be placed on their back, and mark with ink three cauteries according to this shape, and this same quantity, on the lower liver beneath the hypochondria, where the human elbow reaches: and let the space between each cautery be according to the thickness of a finger; and let the cautery be straight according to the length of the body; and do not press your hand with the cautery too much.
And let the quantity of that which is burned be, from the thickness of the skin, the quantity of half of it not added: and let the sick person be standing on their feet.
If, however, he is not standing, then let him be lying down, having already extended his legs and raised his arms.
This is the shape of the cautery.
And it is possible for you, indeed, to cauterize these cauteries with a knife cautery, when you have subtlety and prudence in the art.
And guard yourself so that you do not proceed to the extreme in cauterization, and the thickness of the entire skin is burned, wherefore the whole body is burned, and it reaches the intestines: for the skin there is thin, therefore know that.
Concerning the method of cauterizing abscesses of the liver.
When a discharge occurs, and you wish to know if the abscess is in the flesh of the liver, or in its tunic: then if it is in the flesh of the liver, the patient is afflicted with pain and heaviness without sharpness; and if it is in the tunic of the liver, there is sharp, intense pain; and you see now, that the treatment has fatigued its physicians.
Therefore, the patient should lie on their back upon a pillow. Then mark the site of the abscess with ink; then apply a cautery resembling a ray. And this is its shape. And cauterize with it one cautery, until the entire skin is burned and reaches the pus, until all the pus comes out; then treat it with the treatment for discharges, until it is healed.
And it is not appropriate for one to use this type of cautery unless one's study in the art of medicine is prolonged, and through whose hands these illnesses have come with experience many times; for then may one dare upon such an operation.
But truly, to leave it be, is better in my opinion.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Pleuresia.
The ancients said that cautery with aristolochia roots, for a cold pleurisy, according to this method. And it is that you take from the dry, long aristolochia roots, one root longer than the rest, which is found there, and it should be the thickness of a finger. Then immerse it in oil, and light it in the fire. Then cauterize with one cautery at the point where the fork's junction meets the neck, and with two small cauteries slightly sloping downwards towards the part below the beard.
And with two cauteries also at the point between the fifth and sixth ribs, sloping slightly backwards; and with another cautery in the middle of the chest, and another above the stomach. And with three cauteries from behind: one at the point between the two shoulder blades; and with two cauteries from both sides of the chest, below the cautery which is between the two shoulder blades.
And you should not press your hand with the cautery, but it should be on the skin, clearly smelling.
And some ancients have said that there are men who use a cautery of iron like a ray: and they burn, and thrust it inward into that which is between the ribs, until they reach with it the abscess itself, and pus comes out; just as we have said concerning the abscess of the liver.
But in this perforation with the cautery there is a fear that either the weak person dies immediately, or a fistula occurs in the place, which has no cure.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Spleen, Chapter XXXII.
When you treat the illness of the spleen, with what we have said about treatment in the division of illnesses, and your treatment does not help, then the cautery is used in it according to three methods, which are all correct.
One of which is to make three cauteries, or four, drawing a line along the length of the spleen, according to the shape of the liver cauteries, whose figure preceded.
And let there be between each cautery a quantity equal to the thickness of a finger, or more or less.
And let the method of the cautery be, as we said, in the cautery of the liver, equally.
And do not press your hand with the cautery; and let the weak person be lying on his back.
And another method of cauterization is: that you heat the cautery having two points, which we mentioned in the chapter on the dislocation of the humerus; and elevate the skin, which is directly over the spleen, where the left elbow of the sick person reaches; and let your elevation of the skin be according to the width of the body, so that the cauteries fall along the length of the body.
Then introduce the two very hot points until with them you penetrate the skin on the other side; then withdraw the cautery; therefore four cauteries are made.
And if you wish to cauterize with another cautery having three points.
Then care for the cautery after you let it emit pus for many days; for it is more beneficial than any of the other preceding treatments.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in dropsy.
The cautery does not fall in dropsy, unless properly applied.
When you treat a dropsical patient with the methods of treatment, which we have mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not work, then it is necessary to cauterize him with four cauteries around the navel, and one cautery on the stomach, and another on the liver, and one on the spleen, and two cauteries behind the back between the vertebrae, and one directly on the chest, and another directly on the stomach: and let the depth of the cautery be close to the thickness of the skin.
Then leave the cautery open, so that it discharges pus for a long time.
And do not remove the weak one from treatment after the cautery with that: for it is necessary that two intentions be aggregated to him: and healing will hasten to him with the help of God.
The form of the cautery with which the belly is cauterized should be nail-shaped, according to its previous form; and that with which the back is cauterized should be olive-shaped, according to its previous form.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Feet and Legs.
When ulcers fester in a hydrops patient, and are filled with yellow water, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the foot, in the area between the auricular and annular bones: and raise your hand with the cautery, and do not twist it; then raise your hand again, and do not repeat it at all.
For the yellow water will sweat out, and the cautery should be of this form.
Then, make two cauteries on each leg, and let the cautery be made with the cutting end of the cautery; and let the cautery be made along the length of the leg, one below the knee, and the other below that, approximately in the middle of the leg; and make two cauteries on each thigh; and leave the cautery open without treatment for a long time, so that some water will sweat out from it; then treat it with the rest of the things we have mentioned.
Concerning the method of cauterization in abdominal swelling.
Chapter 35.
When the abdominal swelling is from cold and dampness, weakening the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines; and it is treated with the methods of healing, and is not healed; and you see the sick person tolerating a cautery of abundant strength, then cauterize him with a large cautery on his stomach, according to what preceded in the cauterization of the stomach with a circular cautery, and four small cauteries around the navel, with a small nail cautery; and a large cautery on the hypochondrium, above the other hypochondrium, or with two cauteries.
And if you see excessive moisture, and the sick person tolerating it, then cauterize him with a cautery on the breastbone, and a cautery on each hip; and perhaps add two small cauteries near the large one on the stomach.
For it is a beneficial treatment, whose help does not fail.
Concerning the method of cauterizing Hemorrhoids.
Chapter XXXVI.
When there are many old hemorrhoids in the anus, or one, and they arise from thick, cold humors, or corrupt moisture, and are treated with what we mentioned in the division, and the treatment does not help: then cauterize with three cauteries on the lower spine of the back a little below the navel, triangularly, and with a cautery under the navel as if with two fingers.
And if you think that his stomach is chilled, and his food is not digested, and you see his face become ulcerated, then cauterize him on the stomach with a large cautery, as previously stated: and with a cautery on his liver, and another on his spleen, with a nail-cautery: and leave the cautery open for a time: then treat him until he is healed.
Chapter XXXVII.
When you excise piles, then heat the cautery which is like a ray. Then introduce the heated cautery into the excised pile: and with the back of your hand, until the cautery reaches the opening of the vein through which blood flows: do it once, or twice.
If therefore the piles are numerous, then cauterize each one with the cautery according to what we have described. Then treat them with what you apply from ointments, until they are healed.
And if you cauterize it with a large cautery on the anus, it is more helpful.
Concerning the method of cauterizing a fistula in the anus.
Chapter Thirty-Eight.
When the patient does not submit to the incision and operation we described in its place, and is frightened by it, perhaps he is healed with a cautery.
When therefore a fistula occurs in someone, and it grows old, pus runs from it, and corrupted humors. Therefore, it is more fitting that you probe it with a thin probe. Then determine its depth with the probe.
Then heat the cautery, which is similar to a ray. Then insert the heated cautery into the fistula itself and the amount into which the cautery entered.
And repeatedly apply the cautery to it, until all those corrupted bodies are burned, once, or twice, or thrice, according to your need.
And beware of burning the nerve, if there is one there, or large vein; or if the fistula goes to the bladder, or to the intestines, then beware of all these places.
And do not do it unless the fistula is in a fleshy place, and you think it is not penetrating.
Then treat the place until it is healed.
If however the place is sealed, and the matter is cut away from it, and it remains thus for a long time, then know that it is now healed completely.
And if they do not cut away the matter from it, then know that it is penetrating, or there is a corrupt bone deep within it, or something like that from those things: whose mention will come in its place.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the Kidneys.
When pain in the kidneys occurs from cold or from heavy wind, and it diminishes because of this to the point of weakness of the patient, then it is necessary to cauterize it on the almethen, above the kidneys themselves, cauterizing each kidney with a pointed cauterium, the description of which preceded.
And perhaps we cauterize it a second time on the same almeidatu. Therefore three lines will come. Therefore, the last will be more beneficial.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the bladder.
When weakness and softening of the bladder occur due to cold and moisture, to the point that the patient no longer retains urine, then cauterize it on the lower part of the summit above the bladder, where the hairs of the pubic crest begin. Cauterize from the right side of the summit and another from the left side: and let the length of each cauterization be according to the size of a thumb's width. And cauterize it with an inferior dorsal cautery, or with two cauteries, if you need it. And let it be according to the preceding cauterization.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the womb.
When cold and dampness occur in the womb, and it is prevented from conception, and her menses are corrupted, and their expulsion is delayed, and pain occurs to her upon their arrival, then it is necessary to cauterize it with three cauteries around the navel, as we said in cauterizing the bladder, and with a cautery on the lower back, or with two cauteries.  And let the cautery be of the closing type.
Concerning the method of cauterizing the anus in dislocation.
When mucous humors are discharged into the anus, and become the cause of its exit from its place: and a sign of this is that the leg is prolonged over the other, when they are compared together; and the place of the dislocation is found empty in it.
Therefore, it is necessary to cauterize the afflicted area above the anus itself with a similar circular cautery; after you mark it with ink around the anus, as it revolves; and that the anus itself should fall within the center of the circle.
If this cautery is not present for you, then cauterize it with three cauteries, with a large olive cautery; and let the depth of the cautery be according to the amount of thickness of the entire skin.
Then treat it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Sciatica.
When pain occurs in the hip joint, and its cause is cold and moisture; and the patient is treated with what we have mentioned in the division, and the treatment is not effective, and it is prolonged; then it is necessary to free the patient from the gross humours with foul pills, or with artificial pills, and similar remedies. Then cauterize it.
And the method of cautery in it is according to two methods: either cautery with burning medicines, or cautery with fire.
Cautery with fire, is according to many methods.
One of which is to cauterize above the hip joint itself with three triangular cauteries, according to this form. And make them a good or bad depth. And let the space that is between each cautery be the thickness of a finger: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
Sometimes however, a cautery is made in the middle, over the head of the hip itself. Therefore there are four cauteries.
And if you wish to cauterize with a circle, whose form preceded in the cauterization of the hip dislocation, by one: so that the circle will contain the entire hip.
And burn the thickness of the entire skin.
This is the method of cautery in sciatica, when the pain is adhering to the hip itself, and does not extend to the thigh and leg.
If however it extends to the thigh and leg, then cauterize it with two cauteries upon the thigh, upon the place to which the afflicted person there points, where the pain is, and with your cautery upon the ankle four fingers to the wild side a little while: and let the cautery be a knife-like one.
And let the depth of the cautery be according to the depth of the thickness of the skin.
If the afflicted person indicates that the pain extends nearly to the toes of the foot, then cauterize it there where he indicates with a point cautery, three, or four, or more, if it requires it.
And if he indicates the pain to be below the knee towards the leg, then cauterize it there with one knife-like cautery.
And beware in all your cauterizations, that you do not finish with the cautery so as to burn a nerve, or a great artery, and draw through it upon the afflicted person a bad harm, or contraction.
And I myself have already seen one and another, of those who cauterized above the ankle, and finished in their cauterization, and the leg was swollen, until the swelling reached the foot, and the whole was perforated, and the whole foot was corrupted: then there followed a dissolution of the belly, and death after that.
If the pain is in two parts simultaneously, cauterize each according to this method.
And certain wise men said in cauterization of the buttock, of which cautery this is the method. Make a similar cautery of iron, whose diameter be the half of a palm: and let it be at its opening according to the thickness of a date-stone, or a little less: and within that cautery let there be a third cautery.
And let the space between each cautery be the amount of a thumb's knot: and let the cauteries be open on both sides: and let their height be like one knot, or two knots: and make for them a handle of iron fitting well into the cauteries.
Then let it be heated in fire, until it glows red and throws off sparks: then let it be placed upon the box of the buttock of the sick person lying on their healthy side. Therefore cauterize him with three round cauteries at one time.
Then leave him for three days. Afterwards apply plasters with butter, and leave the wound open for many days. Then treat him with ointment until he is healed.
Albucasis says, "By this kind of cautery, my sons, we have used little, because of the terror of its appearance and because we find few who will wait upon it.
However, it is a good cautery for him who suffers and finds its place with him.
The cautery, however, is with burning medicines, so that you make two samia having a perforated armilla, into which descends the hinge of its door of bronze or iron, the length of a wall; of which in the height of them shall be two knots or like to them.
And let the space between both quantities be the thickness of a finger, and let them be open below and above; and let that which contains them adhere to each other, according to this form.
Then place it upon a box of ashes, the sick person lying upon the healthy side. And press your hand upon the box of ashes forcefully. Then pour between the two circles hot water, which has been warmed a little with fire, and hold it for the amount of an hour: and let the sick person tolerate its scorching, and its burning, for he finds the scorching like fire, until the scorching ceases.
Then raise your hand with the instrument, and wipe away the hot water from the whole ash with fresh water; then leave it for three days.
And put butter upon it, until the blackness of the burning is removed; and leave it for several days, and pus will run from it. For it is the last in assistance.
Then treat it with ointments until it is healed.
If the pain extends to the thigh or leg, make a poultice on it containing water, as you did for the ash equally.
And this is the method of hot water; and I have already written it in the treatise on the rectification of medicines. Take alkali and quicklime, of both one part: grind both, and place them in a new pot, the bottom of which is pierced with one small hole, according to the amount that the ray will enter: and place another glass pot beneath the bottom of the pot: and pour over the alkali and lime with sweet water, so that both are submerged by a finger: after which you press them with your hand with a good pressure: and leave the pot until the sharp water descends into the lower part of the glass pot.
Then collect all that water and pour it over more lime; and strain it until it is renewed.
For it will then be very strong and sharp, which is administered in many surgical operations, and in cauterizing other limbs. Because it produces the effect of fire itself.
And among the medicaments with which incisions are cauterized are also, like tessie, and honey of almonds, and lime with soap, so that both are mixed together.
And Galen, indeed, narrating, recounted the treatment of a certain man from the ancients, with which the pain of the hip and sciatic vein were cured; and he magnified it to be very great. And he said, that he did not need any other treatment, and that he was healed in one instance, until he related, that perhaps he had entered a bath carried, and emerged from it already healthy.
And it is to be taken from green seitaragi; and if green is not found, let dry, fresh, be taken; and it should be thoroughly rubbed with some fat, and placed over the hip, where the pain is, or the leg, or the thigh; and it should be bound, and left for a period of three hours, or for the amount of time the sick person feels the sedation of the burning. Then introduce him into the bath.
When therefore his body becomes moist, introduce him onto the couch. For the pain recedes, and he is healed.
And know that it is not appropriate for anyone to use a cautery with these remedies unless after evacuation of the body.
And Dioscorides also said that the dung of goats, when cauterized with it the sciatic vein, benefits it: and the cautery is done in this way. Take wool, and soak it in old oil, and place it over the deep place, which is between the toe and the heel, and is closer to the heel.
Then take dry goat dung, and ignite it in fire, until it becomes charcoal.
Then place it upon the wool, and leave it until it is extinguished. Then repeat it. Therefore do not cease to do this, until the sensation on the affected area is lessened and the pain subsides.
And this method of cautery is called the Vaccine cautery.
Concerning the cauterization of back pain.
Sometimes pain in the back occurs from many causes, either from an accident, or a blow, or the evacuation of excess fluids, and similar things, from the infusion of cold and moist matter.  A cautery is not applied, however, except in this one case which occurs from the infusion of cold matter.
Therefore, after the patient's evacuation with foul pills and similar remedies, three lines should be made on the back, where the pain is, according to the width of the affected area itself. After marking with ink five cauteries on each line, or more, depending on the patient's tolerance, the cauterization should be performed with the cautery-puncture method.
And if you wish, cauterize with three or four cauteries using the medial cautery-clavil, according to this method.
Concerning the method of cauterization in the beginning stages of a hump.
This illness often occurs in young infants.
And the sign of its beginning in children is that there occurs constriction in their breathing upon raising themselves and moving; and you find in the last thoracic vertebrae and their processes that it has already begun to project above the other vertebrae.
Therefore, when you see it, and wish to treat it, then cauterize it with a cautery that is round, according to this shape.
And let the cautery encompass the entire vertebral part equally; and if you wish to cauterize the vertebral circumference with a pointed cautery, make two or three lines of punctures, and let the punctures be close together.
Then treat the place until it is healed with what we have said.
And beware, lest you administer the cautery to the hump which is formed in nerve spasm.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in gout and joint pains.
When the pains of the joints are from cold humors that are shed into any member of the body, then when pains happen in the feet, it is customary for physicians to properly call it Gout.
Therefore, when gout of a cold cause is treated with methods of cure, and the pains are not removed, then the cautery removes them.
And it is that one should cauterize it after evacuation, in the circumference of the joints of the feet, with many cauteries: and let the cautery be olive-shaped.
And if you need to prick on the surface of the foot, then do so with a pointed cautery. If the pains ascend to the knees, or other joints, and this often happens, then cauterize it above each knee with three or four cauteries, on all sides, with this same claw-shaped cautery.
If, however, more of this cautery is necessary for you, then cauterize it. And do not submerge your hand with the cautery, but let it be about the thickness of the skin only.
If, however, the pains ascend to the knees and back, then administer what we said about the cautery in its chapter.
If the pains are only in the hands, then prick the points in the circumference of the foci, as two lines revolve.
If, however, pain remains in the fingers, then prick them, above each knot, and above the hand's ridge.
If, however, the pains ascend after days to the elbows, or to the shoulders, then cauterize both from every side.
And do not evacuate the sick person from good regimen, from the reception of medicines. For if a good regimen is made, and phlegm is evacuated, it will be healed with the help of God with this cauterization.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in Ruptures.
When a rupture occurs in the groins, and the intestine or the scrotum descends to the testicle, and it is close to starting, then it is necessary that you order the sick person to give up eating on his day. And let him use laxatives, that the stool may descend from his belly.
Then let him sit between your hands on his back; and order him to hold his breath until it emerges, or the scrotum, or the intestine appears.
Then reduce it with your fingers, and mark with ink under the rupture above the pubic bone, with a sign whose extremity is similar to half a circle towards the upper part of the body.
Then cauterize with a cautery, of which this is the form, until it becomes white, and throws off sparks. Then reduce the intestine, or scrotum, to its cavity. Then let the assistant place his hand over the spot, so that the intestine does not come out; and you have now opened between the legs of the sick person, and placed a cushion beneath him, and another servant above his legs, and another above his chest who holds his hands.
Then place the cautery on that mark, your hand holding the cautery standing straight. And hold it until you reach the mouth with it: or repeat it another time with it, if you have not reached the mouth with it the first time.
And carefully observe, during your cauterization, for the exit of the intestine, so that you do not burn it, and that it may result in the patient's death, or great harm.
And know that when you do not reach the mouth with the cautery, your operation is not beneficial.
And the cautery for infants should be slender, according to their size.
Then treat with the remaining ointments, until it is healed.
And let the sick person lie on their back for forty days, until the wound is sealed.
And it is necessary to give him nourishment for the duration of his treatment, that will soothe his belly, so that the intestines will not be discharged during straining and evacuation.
Then when he wants to get up after forty days, then administer a properly made bandage, and let him keep it for another forty days.
And let him lessen labor, and the repletion of food and drink, and loud voices.
For when he uses this regimen, he is thus healed completely.
And I will speak of the treatment of Ruptures with incision in his chapter.
However, when ruptures occur in the rest of the belly, and are beginning, and there is a wish that they not increase, then cauterize the rupture with a round cautery according to its size: and let that which is cauterized be thenceforth like a third of it. Then treat him with what we have said: and it will not increase.
And now some of the first have said that a rupture should be cauterized with a triangular cautery, according to this shape.
After it is marked with ink, and a line is placed which is across the width on the upper side of the Rupture, and another line towards the lower. And place your hand in the middle with the cautery clamp.
But the first cautery is easier and better.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in pains due to a fall or a blow.
Chapter XLVIII.
When, in certain limbs, pain occurs from a fall or blow, and that pain persists for a long time, and treatment with medicines does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize with a pointed cautery.
And let the cautery of every limb be a cautery according to its size, and its smallness, and its weakness, and its strength, and the location of the twisting, and the pain therefrom.
If, therefore, it is healed by the first cautery, it is well. If not, then repeat the cautery upon it.
Because it is customary for these pains to shift from one limb to that which is near it. Therefore, you should pursue them with cautery until the afflicted one is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Leprosy.
Leprosy patients are sometimes greatly helped by cauterization. And especially the kind of leprosy that arises from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy: therefore, when you wish to cauterize it, consider it.
If, therefore, the leprosy is intractable, and you have treated it with what we stated in the division, and it has not subsided or ceased, and you fear that the corruption will spread to the entire constitution of the patient: then cauterize him on the head with five cauteries: one in the middle of the forehead, and a second below it towards the front at the end of the hair, and two above the two temples, and one behind the nape of the neck.
And hold your hand with the cautery for a short time, until a small indentation is impressed on the area, and the outer layers are loosened: so that the expulsion of gross vapors from it may be eased, and cauterize also the spleen with the cautery, according to what has been previously stated.
But if the leprosy has already spread over the patient and is clearly visible: then it is necessary that you cauterize with the cauteries we mentioned on the head, and with a cautery on the tip of the nose, and with two cauteries on the two cheekbones, and with two cauteries on the vertebrae of the neck, and with six on the vertebrae of the back, and with one large one on the haunches near the base of the tail and one above it, in the middle of the buttocks; and with two on the groins, one on each groin, and two on the shoulders, and two on the elbows, and two on the soft parts of his chest; and cauterize him on every joint, from the joints of the fingers of his hands and feet, and cauterize on every heel of his feet, and on the soft parts of his hands.
And beware of the nerves that are above the heel, so that you do not burn them.
And sometimes a cautery is applied to the breastbone, and another to the stomach, and another to the liver.
And know that the more you apply the cautery, the more beneficial and helpful it is.
And know that the patient does not experience pain from the cautery as healthy people do, because his body is already numb.
And there should be cauteries of various sizes, according to the members and joints, according to what has been previously described in the types of instruments.
Then treat the cautery with flour of herbs and honey, and the rest of the treatment, until healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a state of stupor.
When any limb is in a state of stupor, and is treated with medicines, and oils, and plasters, and is not healed, then cauterize that stupified limb with cauteries, according to the merit of its size, whether great or small.
And let your cautery enter into the thickness of the skin a little. Then treat it with ointment, until it is healed.
And sometimes it is cauterized for a kind of stupor which occurs in the hand and foot, in the spinal column of the back at the exit points of the nerves which move that limb: and the stupor is removed.
But let no one presume upon it, unless he is wise in the anatomy of the limbs, and the exit of the moving nerves of the body.
Chapter LI.
When Albaras becomes old and nothing from the arts of medicine helps it, then cauterize over it with a deep cautery for a short time, according to the thickness of the skin, until the whiteness is removed and its colour is changed.
Then treat it with flour of herbs, and lentils with rose oil, and leaves of arnoglossa, and the blood of a dove, and the blood of a swallow: of each one part: let these all be mixed, and be smeared on a cloth, and applied to the place until it heals.
On the method of cauterization in Cancer.
When the Cancer is beginning, and you wish to stop it, then cauterize it with a circular cautery around it, as it revolves.
However, the wise have said that it should be cauterized with the final cautery in the middle.
However, it does not seem right to me, because I fear it will become ulcerated, and I have seen it happen several times.
And it is more correct that it be cauterized around it with a circle, as we said, or with many cauteries.
Concerning the method of cauterization in Adubelati.
When someone has Adubelati, and it is delayed in maturation, either because of an excess causing it, or because of the patient's age, when he is decrepit with little blood, or because of the time, and the need to hasten the maturation of the Adubelati, then cauterize around it with many small cauteries by puncturing. Then leave it. For it will hasten with maturation.
If however you want to perforate it with a cautery, then heat the cautery, of which this is the form.
And place it in the middle of the Adubelati, until it penetrates the skin: and let the cautery be from that which follows the patient, so that the course of the purulent matter may be alleviated.
Then treat it until it is healed.
Concerning the method of cauterization in a corroding evil.
Chapter LIIII.
Corrosion is not except corruption walking in a member, and it corrodes it; just as fire eats dry wood.
If therefore you see corrosion in a place that can tolerate cautery with fire, then apply many cauteries of fire, small and large clamps, according to what will be suitable for the place in which the corrosion is.
Then cauterize it from every part until you eradicate all the corruption, and nothing of it remains at all.
Then leave it for three days, and put powdered sulfur with oil on the cauterized places, until all the eschars and all corruption are eradicated.
Then treat it with ointments that generate flesh.
If therefore you see that after three days healthy flesh is born, in which there is no corruption, it is good.
And if not, then again cauterize that which remains of the corrupted places.
And it is sometimes cured by corroding medicine. For it indeed rises in the place of the cautery.
However, cautery with fire is of quicker benefit; and I have already said that its cauterization with sharp medicine is in division; therefore, take it there when you need it.
Concerning the method of cauterizing in corns and warts.
Chapter LV.
This ailment frequently occurs in the lower parts of the feet, and it is a thick, filtered substance that harms the foot.
And cautery in them is indeed in two ways: cautery with fire, and cautery with hot water.
Concerning the cautery with fire, you should make a concave cautery like a bird of prey's feather, made of iron, the size of the corn all around, and have thin edges.
Then place it, heated, upon the corn. Then revolve the hand with the cautery around the corn, until the cautery reaches the depth of the corn, and leave it for three days, until it begins to discharge pus. Then plaster it with crushed wild mallows and salt, and leave the plaster upon it overnight. For it will be rooted out from its roots.
Then treat the place with a generative flesh ointment until it is healed.
If they are not converted, and often occur on the surface of the body, especially in the hands and feet, then apply a cautery to them with hot water.  And it is, that you should take a cannula of bronze, or iron, or of vulture's feather, and place it upon the corn, or whitlow.
